# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# OpenJDK G1 GC Garbage Collection Cycle Chain

## Your Task

Trace the G1 garbage collector's concurrent marking and mixed collection cycle in openjdk/jdk. Find C++ source files implementing: the G1ConcurrentMark start trigger, the SATB marking queue processing, the remembered set scanning, and the mixed collection region selection.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/jdk--742e735d.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/jdk--742e735d` (openjdk/jdk)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully traced the G1 garbage collector's concurrent marking and mixed collection cycle in openjdk/jdk and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

### 1. **G1ConcurrentMark Start Trigger**
- `G1ConcurrentMark::concurrent_cycle_start()` (g1ConcurrentMark.cpp:1114)
- `G1ConcurrentMark::post_concurrent_mark_start()` (g1ConcurrentMark.cpp:908) activates SATB queues

### 2. **SATB Marking Queue Processing**
- `G1CMTask::drain_satb_buffers()` (g1ConcurrentMark.cpp:2424) processes SATB buffers during concurrent marking
- `G1SATBMarkQueueSet::filter()` (g1SATBMarkQueueSet.cpp:116) filters stale references using TAMS

### 3. **Remembered Set Scanning**
- `G1RemSet::scan_heap_roots()` and `merge_heap_roots()` manage card table scanning
- `G1RemSetScanState` tracks card iteration state across regions
- `G1HeapRegionRemSet` manages individual region remembered sets using `G1CardSet`

### 4. **Mixed Collection Region Selection**
- `G1CollectionSetChooser::build()` (g1CollectionSetChooser.cpp:262) builds candidates in parallel
- `G1BuildCandidateRegionsTask` evaluates regions based on occupancy thresholds
- Regions are sorted by reclaimable bytes and pruned by waste percentage

### 5. **Cycle Orchestration**
- `G1ConcurrentMarkThread::concurrent_mark_cycle_do()` orchestrates 5 major phases:
  1. Scan root regions
  2. Mark loop (mark from roots → preclean → remark)
  3. Rebuild and scrub remembered sets
  4. Cleanup
  5. Clear bitmap for next mark

The complete answer with all files, symbols, and detailed narrative has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

For this, the mark\\n122: // stack memory is split into evenly sized chunks of oops. Users can only\\n123: // add or remove entries on that basis.\\n124: // Chunks are filled in increasing address order. Not completely filled chunks\\n125: // have a null element as a terminating element.\\n126: //\\n127: // Every chunk has a header containing a single pointer element used for memory\\n128: // management. This wastes some space, but is negligible (< .1% with current sizing).\\n129: //\\n130: // Memory management is done using a mix of tracking a high water-mark indicating\\n131: // that all chunks at a lower address are valid chunks, and a singly linked free\\n132: // list connecting all empty chunks.\\n133: class G1CMMarkStack {\\n134: public:\\n135:   // Number of TaskQueueEntries that can fit in a single chunk.\\n136:   static const size_t EntriesPerChunk = 1024 - 1 /* One reference for the next pointer */;\\n137: private:\\n138:   struct TaskQueueEntryChunk {\\n139:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* next;\\n140:     G1TaskQueueEntry data[EntriesPerChunk];\\n141:   };\\n142: \\n143:   class ChunkAllocator {\\n144:     // The chunk allocator relies on a growable array data structure that allows resizing without the\\n145:     // need to copy existing items. The basic approach involves organizing the array into chunks,\\n146:     // essentially creating an \\\"array of arrays\\\"; referred to as buckets in this implementation. To\\n147:     // facilitate efficient indexing, the size of the first bucket is set to a power of 2. This choice\\n148:     // allows for quick conversion of an array index into a bucket index and the corresponding offset\\n149:     // within the bucket. Additionally, each new bucket added to the growable array doubles the capacity of\\n150:     // the growable array.\\n151:     //\\n152:     // Illustration of the growable array data structure.\\n153:     //\\n154:     //        +----+        +----+----+\\n155:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\\n156:     //        |    |        +----+----+\\n157:     //        +----+        +----+----+\\n158:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\\n159:     //        |    |        +----+----+\\n160:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\\n161:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |\\n162:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\\n163:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\\n164:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |    |\\n165:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\\n166:     //        +----+\\n167:     //\\n168:     size_t _min_capacity;\\n169:     size_t _max_capacity;\\n170:     size_t _capacity;\\n171:     size_t _num_buckets;\\n172:     bool _should_grow;\\n173:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* _buckets;\\n174:     char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\\n175:     volatile size_t _size;\\n176:     char _pad4[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(size_t)];\\n177: \\n178:     size_t bucket_size(size_t bucket) {\\n179:       return (bucket == 0) ?\\n180:               _min_capacity :\\n181:               _min_capacity * ( 1ULL << (bucket - 1));\\n182:     }\\n183: \\n184:     static unsigned int find_highest_bit(uintptr_t mask) {\\n185:       return count_leading_zeros(mask) ^ (BitsPerWord - 1U);\\n186:     }\\n187: \\n188:     size_t get_bucket(size_t array_idx) {\\n189:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\\n190:         return 0;\\n191:       }\\n192: \\n193:       return find_highest_bit(array_idx) - find_highest_bit(_min_capacity) + 1;\\n194:     }\\n195: \\n196:     size_t get_bucket_index(size_t array_idx) {\\n197:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\\n198:         return array_idx;\\n199:       }\\n200:       return array_idx - (1ULL << find_highest_bit(array_idx));\\n201:     }\\n202: \\n203:     bool reserve(size_t new_capacity);\\n204: \\n205:   public:\\n206:     ChunkAllocator();\\n207: \\n208:     ~ChunkAllocator();\\n209: \\n210:     bool initialize(size_t initial_capacity, size_t max_capacity);\\n211: \\n212:     void reset() {\\n213:       _size = 0;\\n214:       _should_grow = false;\\n215:     }\\n216: \\n217:     // During G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask or finalize_marking phases, we prefer to restart the marking when\\n218:     // the G1CMMarkStack overflows. Attempts to expand the G1CMMarkStack should be followed with a restart\\n219:     // of the marking. On failure to allocate a new chuck, the caller just returns and forces a restart.\\n220:     // This approach offers better memory utilization for the G1CMMarkStack, as each iteration of the\\n221:     // marking potentially involves traversing fewer unmarked nodes in the graph.\\n222: \\n223:     // However, during the reference processing phase, instead of restarting the marking process, the\\n224:     // G1CMMarkStack is expanded upon failure to allocate a new chunk. The decision between these two\\n225:     // modes of expansion is determined by the _should_grow parameter.\\n226:     void set_should_grow() {\\n227:       _should_grow = true;\\n228:     }\\n229: \\n230:     size_t capacity() const { return _capacity; }\\n231: \\n232:     // Expand the mark stack doubling its size.\\n233:     bool try_expand();\\n234:     bool try_expand_to(size_t desired_capacity);\\n235: \\n236:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* allocate_new_chunk();\\n237:   };\\n238: \\n239:   ChunkAllocator _chunk_allocator;\\n240: \\n241:   char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\\n242:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _free_list;  // Linked list of free chunks that can be allocated by users.\\n243:   char _pad1[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*)];\\n244:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _chunk_list; // List of chunks currently containing data.\\n245:   volatile size_t _chunks_in_chunk_list;\\n246:   char _pad2[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*) - sizeof(size_t)];\\n247: \\n248:   // Atomically add the given chunk to the list.\\n249:   void add_chunk_to_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list, TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n250:   // Atomically remove and return a chunk from the given list. Returns null if the\\n251:   // list is empty.\\n252:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list);\\n253: \\n254:   void add_chunk_to_chunk_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n255:   void add_chunk_to_free_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n256: \\n257:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_chunk_list();\\n258:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_free_list();\\n259: \\n260:  public:\\n261:   G1CMMarkStack();\\n262:   ~G1CMMarkStack() = default;\\n263: \\n264:   // Alignment and minimum capacity of this mark stack in number of oops.\\n265:   static size_t capacity_alignment();\\n266: \\n267:   // Allocate and initialize the mark stack.\\n268:   bool initialize();\\n269: \\n270:   // Pushes the given buffer containing at most EntriesPerChunk elements on the mark\\n271:   // stack. If less than EntriesPerChunk elements are to be pushed, the array must\\n272:   // be terminated with a null.\\n273:   // Returns whether the buffer contents were successfully pushed to the global mark\\n274:   // stack.\\n275:   bool par_push_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\\n276: \\n277:   // Pops a chunk from this mark stack, copying them into the given buffer. This\\n278:   // chunk may contain up to EntriesPerChunk elements. If there are less, the last\\n279:   // element in the array is a null pointer.\\n280:   bool par_pop_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\\n281: \\n282:   // Return whether the chunk list is empty. Racy due to unsynchronized access to\\n283:   // _chunk_list.\\n284:   bool is_empty() const { return _chunk_list == nullptr; }\\n285: \\n286:   size_t capacity() const  { return _chunk_allocator.capacity(); }\\n287: \\n288:   void set_should_grow() {\\n289:     _chunk_allocator.set_should_grow();\\n290:   }\\n291: \\n292:   // Expand the stack, typically in response to an overflow condition\\n293:   void expand();\\n294: \\n295:   // Return the approximate number of oops on this mark stack. Racy due to\\n296:   // unsynchronized access to _chunks_in_chunk_list.\\n297:   size_t size() const { return _chunks_in_chunk_list * EntriesPerChunk; }\\n298: \\n299:   void set_empty();\\n300: \\n301:   // Apply Fn to every oop on the mark stack. The mark stack must not\\n302:   // be modified while iterating.\\n303:   template<typename Fn> void iterate(Fn fn) const PRODUCT_RETURN;\\n304: };\\n305: \\n306: // Root MemRegions are memory areas that contain objects which references are\\n307: // roots wrt to the marking. They must be scanned before marking to maintain the\\n308: // SATB invariant.\\n309: // Typically they contain the areas from TAMS to top of the regions.\\n310: // We could scan and mark through these objects during the concurrent start pause,\\n311: // but for pause time reasons we move this work to the concurrent phase.\\n312: // We need to complete this procedure before we can evacuate a particular region\\n313: // because evacuation might determine that some of these \\\"root objects\\\" are dead,\\n314: // potentially dropping some required references.\\n315: // Root MemRegions comprise of the contents of survivor regions at the end\\n316: // of the GC, and any objects copied into the old gen during GC.\\n317: class G1CMRootMemRegions {\\n318:   // The set of root MemRegions.\\n319:   MemRegion* _root_regions;\\n320:   size_t const _max_regions;\\n321: \\n322:   volatile size_t _num_root_regions; // Actual number of root regions.\\n323: \\n324:   volatile size_t _claimed_root_regions; // Number of root regions currently claimed.\\n325: \\n326:   volatile bool _scan_in_progress;\\n327:   volatile bool _should_abort;\\n328: \\n329:   void notify_scan_done();\\n330: \\n331: public:\\n332:   G1CMRootMemRegions(uint const max_regions);\\n333:   ~G1CMRootMemRegions();\\n334: \\n335:   // Reset the data structure to allow addition of new root regions.\\n336:   void reset();\\n337: \\n338:   void add(HeapWord* start, HeapWord* end);\\n339: \\n340:   // Reset the claiming / scanning of the root regions.\\n341:   void prepare_for_scan();\\n342: \\n343:   // Forces get_next() to return null so that the iteration aborts early.\\n344:   void abort() { _should_abort = true; }\\n345: \\n346:   // Return true if the CM thread are actively scanning root regions,\\n347:   // false otherwise.\\n348:   bool scan_in_progress() { return _scan_in_progress; }\\n349: \\n350:   // Claim the next root MemRegion to scan atomically, or return null if\\n351:   // all have been claimed.\\n352:   const MemRegion* claim_next();\\n353: \\n354:   // The number of root regions to scan.\\n355:   uint num_root_regions() const;\\n356: \\n357:   // Is the given memregion contained in the root regions; the MemRegion must\\n358:   // match exactly.\\n359:   bool contains(const MemRegion mr) const;\\n360: \\n361:   void cancel_scan();\\n362: \\n363:   // Flag that we're done with root region scanning and notify anyone\\n364:   // who's waiting on it. Return true if we had to wait, false otherwise.\\n370:   bool wait_until_scan_finished();\\n371: };\\n372: \\n373: // This class manages data structures and methods for doing liveness analysis in\\n374: // G1's concurrent cycle.\\n375: class G1ConcurrentMark : public CHeapObj<mtGC> {\\n376:   friend class G1CMBitMapClosure;\\n377:   friend class G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask;\\n378:   friend class G1CMDrainMarkingStackClosure;\\n379:   friend class G1CMKeepAliveAndDrainClosure;\\n380:   friend class G1CMRefProcProxyTask;\\n381:   friend class G1CMRemarkTask;\\n382:   friend class G1CMRootRegionScanTask;\\n383:   friend class G1CMTask;\\n384:   friend class G1ConcurrentMarkThread;\\n385: \\n386:   G1ConcurrentMarkThread* _cm_thread; // Task queue set\\n410:   TaskTerminator          _terminator;  // For termination\\n411: \\n412:   // Two sync barriers that are used to synchronize tasks when an\\n413:   // overflow occurs. After they exit it, they re-initialize\\n416:   // their data structures and task 0 re-initializes the global data\\n417:   // structures. Then, they enter the second sync barrier. For this, the mark\n122: // stack memory is split into evenly sized chunks of oops. Users can only\n123: // add or remove entries on that basis.\n124: // Chunks are filled in increasing address order. Not completely filled chunks\n125: // have a null element as a terminating element.\n126: //\n127: // Every chunk has a header containing a single pointer element used for memory\n128: // management. This wastes some space, but is negligible (< .1% with current sizing).\n129: //\n130: // Memory management is done using a mix of tracking a high water-mark indicating\n131: // that all chunks at a lower address are valid chunks, and a singly linked free\n132: // list connecting all empty chunks.\n133: class G1CMMarkStack {\n134: public:\n135:   // Number of TaskQueueEntries that can fit in a single chunk.\n136:   static const size_t EntriesPerChunk = 1024 - 1 /* One reference for the next pointer */;\n137: private:\n138:   struct TaskQueueEntryChunk {\n139:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* next;\n140:     G1TaskQueueEntry data[EntriesPerChunk];\n141:   };\n142: \n143:   class ChunkAllocator {\n144:     // The chunk allocator relies on a growable array data structure that allows resizing without the\n145:     // need to copy existing items. The basic approach involves organizing the array into chunks,\n146:     // essentially creating an \"array of arrays\"; referred to as buckets in this implementation. To\n147:     // facilitate efficient indexing, the size of the first bucket is set to a power of 2. This choice\n148:     // allows for quick conversion of an array index into a bucket index and the corresponding offset\n149:     // within the bucket. Additionally, each new bucket added to the growable array doubles the capacity of\n150:     // the growable array.\n151:     //\n152:     // Illustration of the growable array data structure.\n153:     //\n154:     //        +----+        +----+----+\n155:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\n156:     //        |    |        +----+----+\n157:     //        +----+        +----+----+\n158:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\n159:     //        |    |        +----+----+\n160:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n161:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |\n162:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n163:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n164:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |    |\n165:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n166:     //        +----+\n167:     //\n168:     size_t _min_capacity;\n169:     size_t _max_capacity;\n170:     size_t _capacity;\n171:     size_t _num_buckets;\n172:     bool _should_grow;\n173:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* _buckets;\n174:     char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n175:     volatile size_t _size;\n176:     char _pad4[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(size_t)];\n177: \n178:     size_t bucket_size(size_t bucket) {\n179:       return (bucket == 0) ?\n180:               _min_capacity :\n181:               _min_capacity * ( 1ULL << (bucket - 1));\n182:     }\n183: \n184:     static unsigned int find_highest_bit(uintptr_t mask) {\n185:       return count_leading_zeros(mask) ^ (BitsPerWord - 1U);\n186:     }\n187: \n188:     size_t get_bucket(size_t array_idx) {\n189:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n190:         return 0;\n191:       }\n192: \n193:       return find_highest_bit(array_idx) - find_highest_bit(_min_capacity) + 1;\n194:     }\n195: \n196:     size_t get_bucket_index(size_t array_idx) {\n197:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n198:         return array_idx;\n199:       }\n200:       return array_idx - (1ULL << find_highest_bit(array_idx));\n201:     }\n202: \n203:     bool reserve(size_t new_capacity);\n204: \n205:   public:\n206:     ChunkAllocator();\n207: \n208:     ~ChunkAllocator();\n209: \n210:     bool initialize(size_t initial_capacity, size_t max_capacity);\n211: \n212:     void reset() {\n213:       _size = 0;\n214:       _should_grow = false;\n215:     }\n216: \n217:     // During G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask or finalize_marking phases, we prefer to restart the marking when\n218:     // the G1CMMarkStack overflows. Attempts to expand the G1CMMarkStack should be followed with a restart\n219:     // of the marking. On failure to allocate a new chuck, the caller just returns and forces a restart.\n220:     // This approach offers better memory utilization for the G1CMMarkStack, as each iteration of the\n221:     // marking potentially involves traversing fewer unmarked nodes in the graph.\n222: \n223:     // However, during the reference processing phase, instead of restarting the marking process, the\n224:     // G1CMMarkStack is expanded upon failure to allocate a new chunk. The decision between these two\n225:     // modes of expansion is determined by the _should_grow parameter.\n226:     void set_should_grow() {\n227:       _should_grow = true;\n228:     }\n229: \n230:     size_t capacity() const { return _capacity; }\n231: \n232:     // Expand the mark stack doubling its size.\n233:     bool try_expand();\n234:     bool try_expand_to(size_t desired_capacity);\n235: \n236:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* allocate_new_chunk();\n237:   };\n238: \n239:   ChunkAllocator _chunk_allocator;\n240: \n241:   char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n242:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _free_list;  // Linked list of free chunks that can be allocated by users.\n243:   char _pad1[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*)];\n244:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _chunk_list; // List of chunks currently containing data.\n245:   volatile size_t _chunks_in_chunk_list;\n246:   char _pad2[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*) - sizeof(size_t)];\n247: \n248:   // Atomically add the given chunk to the list.\n249:   void add_chunk_to_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list, TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n250:   // Atomically remove and return a chunk from the given list. They must be scanned before marking to maintain the\n308: // SATB invariant.\n309: // Typically they contain the areas from TAMS to top of the regions.\n310: // We could scan and mark through these objects during the concurrent start pause,\n311: // but for pause time reasons we move this work to the concurrent phase.\n312: // We need to complete this procedure before we can evacuate a particular region\n313: // because evacuation might determine that some of these \"root objects\" are dead,\n314: // potentially dropping some required references.\n315: // Root MemRegions comprise of the contents of survivor regions at the end\n316: // of the GC, and any objects copied into the old gen during GC.\n317: class G1CMRootMemRegions {\n318:   // The set of root MemRegions.\n319:   MemRegion* _root_regions;\n320:   size_t const _max_regions;\n321: \n322:   volatile size_t _num_root_regions;
